  97. No need to pay the big bucks, this works great! I have found through trial and error there's a bit of a learning curve on using these types of lashes. I put a very thin coat of a non-clumping mascara on first and let that dry completely. First coat I get both tubes lined up with the caps undone and in the same hand, with the gel I focus on the base to mid lashes, and then lightly coat with the fibers, let that set up, then re-coat with the gel going to the ends of the lashes, and light coat at the tips, sealing again with the gel, two coats is usually sufficient, why waste it? Also for those who had issues with fibers coming off on the cheeks, that usually means they weren't sealed or too much was used, better to do in light layers.

It's easy enough. Most videos said to apply a layer of your own mascara. I'm not sure why, but I've always done it anyway, so I honestly can't say what would happen if you don't. Then gel, then fibers, and always end with a layer of gel, no matter how many layers you do. It seals in the fibers so they don't flake. I forgot once, and though the flaking wasn't horrible, it did happen. But it's never happened otherwise.<br /><br />This comes with two sets, and lasts quite a long time. I don't wear makeup every day, but maybe 4-5 times a week, and it's lasted me about 2 months per set (4 months total). The only reason I gave it 4 stars instead of 5 is because the effects aren't quite as dramatic as I'd hoped. Better than just regular mascara, definitely, but not quite as dramatic as false eyelashes. Most times you'll have to wear more than one layer to achieve anything that looks like more than just regular mascara.<br /><br />I'm attaching a photo so you can see what I mean. The first time I applied the product, it didn't look much different than my normal mascara. The second time (today) it looked amazing!! So much longer and fuller than normal. I learned a few things from my first application and was less hesitant when applying and it turned out great. I can only assume it will continue to improve as I get more confident.<br /><br />2. Apply 1 coat of regular mascara 1st. Concentrate on the base of your lashes to make them black and full near your skin. When you apply the gel and fibers, stay away from the base of your lashes. If you go too far down, you will get fibers in your eyes. Not only is this uncomfortable, it can't be good for your eyes. Focus the gel and fibers on the middle and ends of your lashes to add length. Don't be afraid to comb over and over through them to make sure your lashes don't look clumpy or like spider legs.<br /><br />3. Don't worry about making a bit of a mess. Loose fibers on your skin can be brushed off and gel can be removed with a q-tip, much like traditional mascara. I applied my regular makeup first, made a huge mess all around my eyes with gel and fibers (but my lashes looked pretty) then removed all the mess without ruining the rest of my makeup.<br /><br />4. The ONLY reason I didn't give 4 stars is that in the picture, it comes with a case, and I only received 4 tubes, no case.   881. Works just as well as the party brand. For best results, apply as follows:<br />Apply a thin coat of your regular mascara (powder too if you tend to have runny mascara during the day). Be sure to separate your lashes as you normally do. Let dry.<br />Do only one eye at a time. Apply adhesive (this smells like glue, chemical like, and although I have had no problems, I am very careful about not letting the tip have a glob on it that could get into my eye. I also use my normal mascara to thicken up the base of my lashes, and use this more for the middle and ends.)<br />Apply lashes. Then apply adhesive again (seal in the coat of the lashes.)<br />Do the other eye...check them out...decide if you need/want another coat. Repeat.<br /><br />You can do the lower lashes, but I find them too babydoll looking (falsies), which doesn't work for the workday.<br />You can also play. For example, I am attentive about the outer tops/bottom lashes, and I tend to do a second or third coat just on them to make them fan out...but only the last 1/5 of my eyelid.<br /><br />Most of all, practice. Each time you will get better...oh, and keep a brush from an old mascara, clean well, and use to help separate/clean up when you accidentally get a big clump.<br /><br />I tried 4 different versions of this by different manufacturers and will be giving the same post/review to all because in my opinion they all do the same job well...HOWEVER...I gave this one 5-stars versus the others 4 because it is the least chemically smelling to me (or at least the smell dissipated the fastest, and I've like the results from day 1).   882. I purchased this product because I was running low on another brand and this one was (2) sets for a lower price. I am really pleased with this brand. The gel is a bit more glue/string like than I would like but now that I have used it a few time I got the hang out it, it really isn't an issue. I am a contact lense wearer and I have not had an issue with this brand irritating my eyes. To apply it, I use the following steps and it works out well for me.<br />1. Apply (1) coat of a regular cheapy mascara<br />2. Apply the transplanting gel on top of that<br />3. While the gel is still wet apply the transplanting fibers.<br />4. Let the fibers and the gel dry for about a minute and then apply another coat of the transplanting gel on top of that.<br />5. If you don't feel your lashes are as full or long as you would like, apply another coat of the fibers, let dry for a minute and then add another coat of transplanting gel.<br />6. Repeat on the other eye.<br /><br />I have found that the above steps really help keep the fiber fall out to a minimum. The other trick I have is, keep your eye slightly closed when applying the fibers. If you have your eyes wide open, you will probably get some fibers in your eye.
